04/15/2026 18:09:01 - INFO - __main__ - For `While its primary benefit is improving the generalization ability of the model, it can also have several side effects, both desirable and undesirable [2].`, find citations [2]

1.`, find citations []
04/15/2026 18:09:01 - INFO - __main__ - For `**Ensemble Effect**: Dropout can be interpreted as training an ensemble of subnetworks, each with a different set of active neurons [3].`, find citations [3]
04/15/2026 18:09:01 - INFO - __main__ - For `This ensemble averaging effect can lead to a more robust and less sensitive model to the specific training data [4].`, find citations [4]
04/15/2026 18:09:01 - INFO - __main__ - For `**Implicit Regularization**: Dropout can be seen as a form of implicit regularization, where the network is forced to learn features that are robust to the random dropping of neurons [5].`, find citations [5]
04/15/2026 18:09:01 - INFO - __main__ - For `This can lead to a model that is less reliant on specific features and more capable of capturing the underlying structure of the data [6].`, find citations [6]
04/15/2026 18:09:01 - INFO - __main__ - For `**Improved Optimization**: Dropout can help the network escape sharp minima in the loss landscape, leading to flatter minima that generalize better to unseen data [7].`, find citations [7]
04/15/2026 18:09:01 - INFO - __main__ - For `This is because the network is encouraged to learn functions that are less sensitive to the specific initialization of the weights [8].`, find citations [8]
04/15/2026 18:09:01 - INFO - __main__ - For `**Increased Model Capacity**: While dropout is a form of regularization, it can also be viewed as increasing the effective model capacity [9].`, find citations [9]
04/15/2026 18:09:01 - INFO - __main__ - For `By randomly setting some activations to zero during training, it forces the network to learn more redundant representations, which can improve its ability to capture complex patterns in the data [10].`, find citations [10]

1.`, find citations []
04/15/2026 18:09:01 - INFO - __main__ - For `Sparse Table [1]: A Sparse Table is a static data structure that allows for $O(1)$ query time after $O(N \log N)$ preprocessing time, where $N$ is the size of the array.`, find citations [1]
04/15/2026 18:09:01 - INFO - __main__ - For `It is built using dynamic programming, where $ST[i][j]$ stores the minimum value in the range $[i, i + 2^j - 1]$.`, find citations []
04/15/2026 18:09:01 - INFO - __main__ - For `This table can be precomputed in $O(N \log N)$ time and queried in $O(1)$ time using the property that any range $[L, R]$ can be covered by two overlapping power-of-two segments, $[L, L + 2^k - 1]$ and $[R - 2^k + 1, R]$, where $k = \lfloor \log_2(R - L + 1) \rfloor$.`, find citations []
04/15/2026 18:09:01 - INFO - __main__ - For `Segment Tree [2]: A Segment Tree is a dynamic data structure that supports both range minimum query and point update operations in $O(\log N)$ time.`, find citations [2]
04/15/2026 18:09:01 - INFO - __main__ - For `It is built in $O(N)$ time and allows for $O(\log N)$ query time.`, find citations []

04/15/2026 18:09:01 - INFO - __main__ - For `The tree is built recursively, where the left child covers $[i, mid]$ and the right child covers $[mid + 1, j]$.`, find citations []
04/15/2026 18:09:01 - INFO - __main__ - For `A query for the minimum value in $[L, R]$ is answered by combining the results from the nodes that cover this range.`, find citations []

04/15/2026 18:09:01 - INFO - __main__ - For `The tree is built in $O(N)$ time and supports $O(\log N)$ query time.`, find citations []

04/15/2026 18:09:01 - INFO - __main__ - For `A smaller $\epsilon$ indicates a stronger privacy guarantee, meaning that the output of the mechanism is nearly identical whether or not the input of the mechanism was included in the dataset [2].`, find citations [2]
